<span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Middlesbrough&amp;params=54.5767_N_1.2355_W_region:GB_type:city(174700)"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">54°34′36″N</span> <span class="longitude">1°14′08″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">54.5767°N 1.2355°W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">54.5767; -1.2355</span></span></span></a></span><span style="font-size: small;"><span id="coordinates"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a>: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Middlesbrough&amp;params=54.5767_N_1.2355_W_region:GB_type:city(174700)"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">54°34′36″N</span> <span class="longitude">1°14′08″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">54.5767°N 1.2355°W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">54.5767; -1.2355</span></span></span></a></span></span></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Middlesbrough</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/əl/: &#39;le&#39; in &#39;bottle&#39;">əl</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-uk-Middlesbrough.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/87/En-uk-Middlesbrough.ogg" class="internal" title="En-uk-Middlesbrough.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">MID</span>-əlz-brə</i></a>) is a large post-industrial town<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> on the south bank of the <a href="/wiki/River_Tees" title="River Tees">River Tees</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Yorkshire" title="North Yorkshire">North Yorkshire</a>, northeast <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, founded in 1830.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The local council, a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authority" title="Unitary authority">unitary authority</a>, is <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_Borough_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Middlesbrough Borough Council">Middlesbrough Borough Council</a>. The <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2011">2011 Census</a> recorded the borough's total resident population as 138,400 and the wider urban settlement with a population of 174,700, technically making Middlesbrough the largest urban subdivision in the ceremonial county of North Yorkshire.<sup id="cite_ref-Census2011_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2011-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Middlesbrough is part of the larger built-up area of <a href="/wiki/Teesside" title="Teesside">Teesside</a> which had an overall population of 376,333 at the 2011 Census.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Middlesbrough became a <a href="/wiki/County_borough" title="County borough">county borough</a> within the <a href="/wiki/North_Riding_of_Yorkshire" title="North Riding of Yorkshire">North Riding of Yorkshire</a> in 1889. In 1968, the borough was merged with a number of others to form the <a href="/wiki/County_Borough_of_Teesside" title="County Borough of Teesside">County Borough of Teesside</a>, which was absorbed in 1974 by the county of <a href="/wiki/Cleveland,_England" title="Cleveland, England">Cleveland</a>. In 1996, Cleveland was abolished, and Middlesbrough Borough Council became a unitary authority within North Yorkshire.
RGs
<i>Erimus</i> ("We shall be" in <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>) was chosen as Middlesbrough's motto in 1830. It recalls <i>Fuimus</i> ("We have been") the motto of the Norman/Scottish <a href="/wiki/Bruce_clan" class="mw-redirect" title="Bruce clan">Bruce</a> family, who were lords of Cleveland in the Middle Ages. The town's <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> is an azure lion, from the arms of the Bruce family, a star, from the arms of <a href="/wiki/Captain_James_Cook" class="mw-redirect" title="Captain James Cook">Captain James Cook</a>, and two ships, representing shipbuilding and maritime trade.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="toclimit-3"><div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span></h3>
<p>In 686, a monastic cell was consecrated by <a href="/wiki/Cuthbert_of_Lindisfarne" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuthbert of Lindisfarne">St. Cuthbert</a> at the request of <a href="/wiki/Hilda_of_Whitby" title="Hilda of Whitby">St. Hilda</a>, Abbess of <a href="/wiki/Whitby" title="Whitby">Whitby</a> and in 1119 <a href="/wiki/Robert_de_Brus,_1st_Lord_of_Annandale" title="Robert de Brus, 1st Lord of Annandale">Robert Bruce, Lord of Cleveland and Annandale</a>, granted and confirmed the church of St. Hilda of Middleburg to <a href="/wiki/Whitby" title="Whitby">Whitby</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Up until its closure on the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Monasteries" title="Dissolution of the Monasteries">Dissolution of the Monasteries</a> by <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">Henry VIII</a> in 1537,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> the church was maintained by 12&#160;<a href="/wiki/Benedictine" class="mw-redirect" title="Benedictine">Benedictine</a> monks, many of whom became vicars, or rectors, of various places in Cleveland. The importance of the early church at "Middleburg", later known as <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_Priory" title="Middlesbrough Priory">Middlesbrough Priory</a>, is indicated by the fact that, in 1452, it possessed four altars.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Angles</a>, the area became home to <a href="/wiki/Viking" class="mw-redirect" title="Viking">Viking</a> settlers. Names of Viking origin (with the suffix <i>by</i>) are abundant in the area – for example, <a href="/wiki/Ormesby" title="Ormesby">Ormesby</a>, Stainsby, <a href="/wiki/Maltby,_North_Yorkshire" title="Maltby, North Yorkshire">Maltby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tollesby" title="Tollesby">Tollesby</a> were once separate villages that belonged to <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Vikings</a> called Orm, Steinn, Malti and Toll, but now form suburbs of Middlesbrough. The name Mydilsburgh is the earliest recorded form of Middlesbrough's name and dates from the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Saxon">Anglo-Saxon</a> era (AD 410–1066), while many of the aforementioned villages are recorded in the <a href="/wiki/Domesday_Book" title="Domesday Book">Domesday Book</a> of 1086.
</p><p>Other links persist in the area, often through school or road names, to now-outgrown or abandoned local settlements, such as the <a href="/wiki/Medieval" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval">medieval</a> settlement of Stainsby, <a href="/wiki/Deserted_medieval_village" class="mw-redirect" title="Deserted medieval village">deserted</a> by 1757, which amounts to little more today than a series of grassy mounds near the <a href="/wiki/A19_road" title="A19 road">A19 road</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Middlesbrough_Town_Hall_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Old_Middlesbrough_Town_Hall_2013.jpg/220px-Old_Middlesbrough_Town_Hall_2013.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Old_Middlesbrough_Town_Hall_2013.jpg/330px-Old_Middlesbrough_Town_Hall_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Old_Middlesbrough_Town_Hall_2013.jpg/440px-Old_Middlesbrough_Town_Hall_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="717" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Middlesbrough_Town_Hall_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Old Town Hall</div></div></div>
<p>In 1801, Middlesbrough was a small farm with a population of just 25. During the latter half of the 19th century, however, it experienced rapid growth.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Stockton_and_Darlington_Railway" title="Stockton and Darlington Railway">Stockton and Darlington Railway (S&amp;DR)</a> had been developed to transport coal from <a href="/wiki/Witton_Park_Colliery" title="Witton Park Colliery">Witton Park Colliery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shildon_railway_station" title="Shildon railway station">Shildon</a> in County Durham, to the <a href="/wiki/River_Tees" title="River Tees">River Tees</a> in the east. It had always been assumed by the investors that <a href="/wiki/Stockton_railway_station_(County_Durham)" title="Stockton railway station (County Durham)">Stockton</a> as the then lowest bridging point on the River Tees would be suitable to take the largest ships at the required volume. However, as the trade developed, and with competition from the <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Railway" title="Clarence Railway">Clarence Railway</a> which had established a new port on the north side of the river at <a href="/wiki/Port_Clarence" title="Port Clarence">Port Clarence</a>, a better solution was required on the south side of the river.
</p><p>In 1828 the influential <a href="/wiki/Quaker" class="mw-redirect" title="Quaker">Quaker</a> banker, coal mine owner and S&amp;DR shareholder <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Pease_(railway_pioneer)" title="Joseph Pease (railway pioneer)">Joseph Pease</a> sailed up the River Tees to find a suitable new site down river of Stockton on which to place new coal <a href="/wiki/Staithe" class="mw-redirect" title="Staithe">staithes</a>. As a result, in 1829 he and a group of Quaker businessmen bought the Middlesbrough farmstead and associated estate, some 527 acres (213&#160;ha) of land, and established the Middlesbrough Estate Company. Through the company, the investors set about the development of a new coal port on the banks of the Tees nearby, and a suitable town on the site of the farm (the new town of Middlesbrough) to supply the port with labour. By 1830 the S&amp;DR had been extended to Middlesbrough and expansion of the town was assured. The small farmstead became the site of such streets as North Street, South Street, West Street, East Street, Commercial Street, Stockton Street and Cleveland Street, laid out in a grid-iron pattern around a market square, with the first house being built in West Street in April 1830.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The town of Middlesbrough was born.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> New businesses quickly bought up premises and plots of land in the new town and soon shippers, merchants, butchers, innkeepers, joiners, blacksmiths, tailors, builders and painters were moving in. By 1851 Middlesbrough's population had grown from 40 people in 1829 to 7,600.<sup id="cite_ref-englandsnortheast.co.uk_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-englandsnortheast.co.uk-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first coal shipping staithes at the port (known as "Port Darlington") were constructed just to the west of the site earmarked for the location of Middlesbrough.<sup id="cite_ref-GazDock_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GazDock-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The port was linked to the S&amp;DR on 27 December 1830 via a branch that extended to an area just north of the current <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_railway_station" title="Middlesbrough railway station">Middlesbrough</a> railway station.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The success of the port meant it soon became overwhelmed by the volume of imports and exports, and in 1839 work started on Middlesbrough Dock. Laid out by <a href="/wiki/William_Cubitt" title="William Cubitt">Sir William Cubitt</a>, the whole infrastructure was built by resident <a href="/wiki/Civil_engineer" title="Civil engineer">civil engineer</a> <a href="/wiki/George_Turnbull_(civil_engineer)" title="George Turnbull (civil engineer)">George Turnbull</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GazDock_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GazDock-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> After three years and an expenditure of £122,000 (equivalent to £9.65&#160;million at 2011 prices),<sup id="cite_ref-GazDock_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GazDock-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> first water was let in on 19 March 1842, and the formal opening took place on 12 May 1842. On completion, the docks were bought by the S&amp;DR.<sup id="cite_ref-GazDock_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GazDock-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrialisation">Industrialisation</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Bolckow_Vaughan" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolckow Vaughan">Bolckow Vaughan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dorman_Long" title="Dorman Long">Dorman Long</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ironopolis_wall.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Ironopolis_wall.JPG/220px-Ironopolis_wall.JPG" width="220" height="68" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Ironopolis_wall.JPG/330px-Ironopolis_wall.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Ironopolis_wall.JPG/440px-Ironopolis_wall.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3166" data-file-height="982" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ironopolis_wall.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A wall celebrating the name Ironopolis</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ironstone" title="Ironstone">Ironstone</a> was discovered in the <a href="/wiki/Eston_Nab" title="Eston Nab">Eston Hills</a> in 1850. In 1841, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Bolckow" title="Henry Bolckow">Henry Bolckow</a>, who had come to England in 1827, formed a partnership with <a href="/wiki/John_Vaughan_(Middlesbrough)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Vaughan (Middlesbrough)">John Vaughan</a>, originally of <a href="/wiki/Worcester" title="Worcester">Worcester</a>, and started an <a href="/wiki/Iron_foundry" class="mw-redirect" title="Iron foundry">iron foundry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rolling_mill" class="mw-redirect" title="Rolling mill">rolling mill</a> at Vulcan Street in the town. It was Vaughan who realised the economic potential of local ironstone deposits. <a href="/wiki/Pig_iron" title="Pig iron">Pig iron</a> production rose tenfold between 1851 and 1856. The importance of the area to the developing iron and steel trade gave it the nickname "Ironopolis".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ballarat_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ballarat-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 21 January 1853, Middlesbrough received its <a href="/wiki/Royal_Charter" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Charter">Royal Charter of Incorporation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> giving the town the right to have a mayor, aldermen and councillors. Henry Bolckow became mayor, in 1853.
</p><p>On 15 August 1867, a Reform Bill was passed, making Middlesbrough a new parliamentary borough, Bolckow was elected member for Middlesbrough the following year.
</p><p>For many years in the 19th&#160;century, <a href="/wiki/Teesside" title="Teesside">Teesside</a> set the world price for iron and steel.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="reliable source needed for the whole sentence (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The steel components of the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Harbour_Bridge" title="Sydney Harbour Bridge">Sydney Harbour Bridge</a> (1932) were engineered and fabricated by <a href="/wiki/Dorman_Long" title="Dorman Long">Dorman Long</a> of Middlesbrough. The company was also responsible for the <a href="/wiki/Tyne_Bridge" title="Tyne Bridge">New Tyne Bridge</a> in <a href="/wiki/Newcastle-upon-Tyne" class="mw-redirect" title="Newcastle-upon-Tyne">Newcastle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DLong201407_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DLong201407-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Several large shipyards also lined the Tees, including the <a href="/wiki/Sir_Raylton_Dixon" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Raylton Dixon">Sir Raylton Dixon &amp; Company</a>, which produced hundreds of steam freighters including the infamous <a href="/wiki/SS_Mont-Blanc" title="SS Mont-Blanc">SS Mont-Blanc</a>, the steamship which caused the 1917 <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Explosion" title="Halifax Explosion">Halifax Explosion</a> in Canada.
</p><p>Middlesbrough's rapid expansion continued throughout the second half of the 19th&#160;century (fuelled by the iron and steel industry), the population reaching 90,000 by the turn of the century.<sup id="cite_ref-englandsnortheast.co.uk_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-englandsnortheast.co.uk-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The population of Middlesbrough as a county borough peaked at almost 165,000 in the late 1960s, but has declined since the early 1980s. The 2011 Census recorded the borough's total resident population as 138,400.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Irish_migration_to_Middlesbrough">Irish migration to Middlesbrough</span></h3>
<p>The 1871 census of England &amp; Wales showed that Middlesbrough had the second highest percentage of <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irish</a> born people in England after Liverpool.<sup id="cite_ref-two_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-two-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-three_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-three-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> This equated to 9.2% of the overall population of the district at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-four_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-four-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Due to the rapid development of the town and its industrialisation there was much need for people to work in the many blast furnaces and steel works along the banks of the Tees. This attracted many people from Ireland, who were in much need of work. As well as people from Ireland, the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_people" title="Scottish people">Scottish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Welsh_people" title="Welsh people">Welsh</a> and overseas inhabitants made up 16% of Middlesbrough's population in 1871.<sup id="cite_ref-three_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-three-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Middlesbrough&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(May 2014)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Business in Middlesbrough is still dominated by the nearby <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">chemical industry</a> which until 1995 in this locality was largely owned by <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Chemical_Industries" title="Imperial Chemical Industries">Imperial Chemical Industries</a> (ICI). The fragmentation of that company led to many smaller manufacturing units being owned and operated by a number of multinational organisations. The last part of ICI itself completely left the area in 2006 and the remaining companies are now members of the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_of_England_Process_Industry_Cluster" class="mw-redirect" title="Northeast of England Process Industry Cluster">Northeast of England Process Industry Cluster</a> (NEPIC).
</p><p>The port of <a href="/wiki/Teesport" title="Teesport">Teesport</a>, owned by PD Ports, is also vital to the economy of Middlesbrough and the port owners have their offices in the town. Teesport is 5.5 miles (9&#160;km) from the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> and 3 miles (5&#160;km) east of Middlesbrough, on the <a href="/wiki/River_Tees" title="River Tees">River Tees</a>. Teesport is currently the third largest port in the United Kingdom, and amongst the tenth biggest in Western Europe, handling about 50 million tonnes of domestic and international cargo per year.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The vast majority of these products are still related to the <a href="/wiki/Steel_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Steel industry">steel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">chemical industries</a> made by companies that are members of NEPIC. NEPIC is an industry led <a href="/wiki/Economic_cluster" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic cluster">economic cluster</a> body that promotes the development and growth of the chemistry based <a href="/wiki/Process_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Process industry">process industries</a> around the <a href="/wiki/Tees_Valley" title="Tees Valley">Tees Valley</a> and the wider region of <a href="/wiki/Northeast_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Northeast England">Northeast England</a>.
</p><p>Middlesbrough also remains a stronghold for engineering based manufacturing and engineering contract service businesses. It also has a growing reputation for developing digital businesses particularly in the field of <a href="/wiki/Digital_animation" class="mw-redirect" title="Digital animation">digital animation</a> as a result of spin-out activity in this new industry from the Middlesbrough-based <a href="/wiki/Teesside_University" title="Teesside University">Teesside University</a>.
</p><p>Middlesbrough is served by its town centre which consists of four shopping centres, the largest of which is the Cleveland Centre. The pedestrianised section of Linthorpe Road includes House of Fraser and Debenhams. The town centre has a variety of stores from high street chains to aspirational and lifestyle brands.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">Second World War</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_during_World_War_II" title="Middlesbrough during World War II">Middlesbrough during World War II</a></div>
<p>Middlesbrough was the first major British town and industrial target to be bombed during the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>. The steel making capacity and railways for carrying steel products were obvious targets. The <a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a> first bombed the town on 25 May 1940, when a lone bomber dropped 13 bombs between South Bank Road and the South Steel plant.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> More bombing occurred throughout the course of the war, with the <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_railway_station" title="Middlesbrough railway station">railway station</a> put out of action for two weeks in 1942.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By the end of the war over 200 buildings had been destroyed within the Middlesbrough area. Areas of early and mid-Victorian housing were demolished and much of central Middlesbrough was redeveloped. Heavy industry was relocated to areas of land better suited to the needs of modern technology. Middlesbrough itself began to take on a completely different look.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_Howards">Green Howards</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Green_Howards" class="mw-redirect" title="The Green Howards">The Green Howards</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Green_Howards" title="Green Howards">Green Howards</a> was a <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a> infantry regiment very strongly associated with Middlesbrough and the area south of the River Tees. Originally formed at <a href="/wiki/Dunster_Castle" title="Dunster Castle">Dunster Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somerset" title="Somerset">Somerset</a> in 1688 to serve King William of Orange, later <a href="/wiki/William_III_of_England" title="William III of England">King William III</a>, this famous regiment became affiliated to the <a href="/wiki/North_Riding_of_Yorkshire" title="North Riding of Yorkshire">North Riding of Yorkshire</a> in 1782. As Middlesbrough grew, its population of men came to be a group most targeted by the recruiters. The Green Howards were part of the <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Division" title="King&#39;s Division">King's Division</a>. On 6 June 2006, this famous regiment was merged into the new <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Regiment" title="Yorkshire Regiment">Yorkshire Regiment</a> and are now known as 2 Yorks – The 2nd Battalion The Yorkshire Regiment (Green Howards). There is also a <a href="/wiki/Territorial_Army_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Territorial Army (United Kingdom)">Territorial Army</a> (TA) company at Stockton Road in Middlesbrough, part of 4 Yorks which is wholly reserve.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span></h2>
<table class="wikitable" style="float:right; margin-right:30px">

<td>Edgar Gilkes

<p>Middlesbrough was incorporated as a <a href="/wiki/Municipal_borough" title="Municipal borough">municipal borough</a> in 1853. It extended its boundaries in 1866 and 1887, and became a <a href="/wiki/County_borough" title="County borough">county borough</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1888" title="Local Government Act 1888">Local Government Act 1888</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_Rural_District" title="Middlesbrough Rural District">Middlesbrough Rural District</a> was formed in 1894, covering a rural area to the south of the town. It was abolished in 1932, partly going to the county borough; but mostly going to the <a href="/wiki/Stokesley_Rural_District" title="Stokesley Rural District">Stokesley Rural District</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1968 Middlesbrough became part of the <a href="/wiki/County_Borough_of_Teesside" title="County Borough of Teesside">County Borough of Teesside</a>, and in 1974 it became part of the non-metropolitan county of <a href="/wiki/Cleveland,_England" title="Cleveland, England">Cleveland</a> until the county's abolition in 1996, when Middlesbrough became a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authority" title="Unitary authority">unitary authority</a>. The town now forms part of <a href="/wiki/North_Yorkshire" title="North Yorkshire">North Yorkshire</a> for ceremonial purposes only.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h3>
<p>Currently the <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Middlesbrough (UK Parliament constituency)">Middlesbrough constituency</a> is represented by <a href="/wiki/Andy_McDonald_(politician)" title="Andy McDonald (politician)">Andy McDonald</a> for Labour in the House of Commons. He was elected in a <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_by-election,_2012" title="Middlesbrough by-election, 2012">by-election</a> held on 29 November 2012 following the death of previous Member of Parliament <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Bell" title="Stuart Bell">Sir Stuart Bell</a>, who was the MP since 1983.
</p><p>Middlesbrough has been a traditionally safe <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> seat. The first Conservative MP for Middlesbrough was Sir <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Alexander_Sadler" class="mw-redirect" title="Samuel Alexander Sadler">Samuel Alexander Sadler</a>, elected in 1900.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_Government">Local Government</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_Council" title="Middlesbrough Council">Middlesbrough Council</a></div>
<dl><dt>Mayor</dt></dl>
<p>In 2002, Middlesbrough voted to have a <a href="/wiki/Elected_mayors_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Elected mayors in the United Kingdom">directly elected</a> mayor as head of the council. <a href="/wiki/Ray_Mallon" title="Ray Mallon">Ray Mallon</a> (independent), formerly a senior officer in Cleveland Police was the first elected mayor, serving three terms of office beginning in 2002, 2007 and 2011. In May 2015, after Mallon stated he would not contest a fourth term, Dave Budd (Labour) was voted in, narrowly defeating Andy Preston (independent).<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Before having an elected mayor, the council had a ceremonial mayor. The functions of this office have been transferred to the office of "Chair of Middlesbrough Council".
</p><p>The first Mayor of Middlesbrough was the German-born <a href="/wiki/Henry_Bolckow" title="Henry Bolckow">Henry Bolckow</a> in 1853.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In the 20th century, encompassing introduction of <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> in 1918 and changes in <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Local government in the United Kingdom">local government in the United Kingdom</a>, the role of mayor changed. Unlike some other places with a "City Mayor" and "Ceremonial Mayor", the traditional civic and ceremonial functions of the Mayor, including mayoral chains and robes, are now vested with the role now called 'Chair of Middlesbrough Council'. The Chair is still chosen by the Council from among the elected Councillors.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OS_map_Middlesbrough-Stockton_area.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/OS_map_Middlesbrough-Stockton_area.png/220px-OS_map_Middlesbrough-Stockton_area.png" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/OS_map_Middlesbrough-Stockton_area.png/330px-OS_map_Middlesbrough-Stockton_area.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/OS_map_Middlesbrough-Stockton_area.png/440px-OS_map_Middlesbrough-Stockton_area.png 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="473" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OS_map_Middlesbrough-Stockton_area.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the Middlesbrough / Stockton-on-Tees area</div></div></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<p>Middlesbrough has an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> typical for the United Kingdom.
Being sheltered from prevailing south-westerly winds by both the <a href="/wiki/Lake_District" title="Lake District">Lake District</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennines</a> to the west and the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Hills" title="Cleveland Hills">Cleveland Hills</a> to the south, Middlesbrough is in one of the relatively drier parts of the country, receiving on average 574 millimetres (22.6 inches) of rain a year. Temperatures range from mild summer highs in July and August typically around 20&#160;°C (68&#160;°F) to winter lows in December and January falling to around 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3>
<p>Middlesbrough is served well by public transport. Locally, <a href="/wiki/Arriva_North_East" title="Arriva North East">Arriva North East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_Group" title="Stagecoach Group">Stagecoach</a> provide the majority of bus services, with <a href="/wiki/National_Express_Coaches" title="National Express Coaches">National Express</a> and <a href="/wiki/Megabus_(Europe)" title="Megabus (Europe)">Megabus</a> operating long distance coach travel from <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_bus_station" title="Middlesbrough bus station">Middlesbrough bus station</a>.
</p><p>Train services are operated by <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a> and <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a>. Departing from <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_railway_station" title="Middlesbrough railway station">Middlesbrough railway station</a>, Northern operates rail services throughout the north-east region including to <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sunderland,_Tyne_and_Wear" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunderland, Tyne and Wear">Sunderland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darlington" title="Darlington">Darlington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Redcar" title="Redcar">Redcar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whitby" title="Whitby">Whitby</a>, whilst TransPennine Express provides direct rail services to cities such as <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/York" title="York">York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>.
</p><p>Middlesbrough is served by a number of major roads including the <a href="/wiki/A19_road" title="A19 road">A19</a> (north/south), <a href="/wiki/A66_road" title="A66 road">A66</a> (east/west), <a href="/wiki/A171_road" title="A171 road">A171</a>, <a href="/wiki/A172_road_(England)" title="A172 road (England)">A172</a> and <a href="/wiki/A174_road" title="A174 road">A174</a>.
</p><p>In the past Middlesbrough has been served by the <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough,_Stockton_and_Thornaby_Electric_Tramways_Company" title="Middlesbrough, Stockton and Thornaby Electric Tramways Company">Middlesbrough, Stockton and Thornaby Electric Tramways Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Tramways_Company" title="Imperial Tramways Company">Imperial Tramways Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_Corporation_Tramways" title="Middlesbrough Corporation Tramways">Middlesbrough Corporation Tramways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Teesside" title="Trolleybuses in Teesside">Tees-side Railless Traction Board</a> and <a href="/wiki/County_Borough_of_Teesside#Teesside_Municipal_Transport" title="County Borough of Teesside">Teesside Municipal Transport</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">Landmarks</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AcklamHall_Grounds1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/AcklamHall_Grounds1.jpg/250px-AcklamHall_Grounds1.jpg" width="250" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/AcklamHall_Grounds1.jpg/375px-AcklamHall_Grounds1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/AcklamHall_Grounds1.jpg/500px-AcklamHall_Grounds1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="907" data-file-height="591" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AcklamHall_Grounds1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Acklam Hall</div></div></div>
<p>In the suburb and former village of Acklam, Middlesbrough's oldest domestic building is <a href="/wiki/Acklam_Hall" title="Acklam Hall">Acklam Hall</a> of 1678. Built by Sir <a href="/wiki/William_Hustler_(draper)" class="mw-redirect" title="William Hustler (draper)">William Hustler</a>, it is also Middlesbrough's sole <a href="/wiki/Listed_building#Categories_of_listed_building" title="Listed building">Grade I listed building</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/English_Restoration" class="mw-redirect" title="English Restoration">Restoration</a> <a href="/wiki/Mansion" title="Mansion">mansion</a>, accessible through an avenue of trees off Acklam Road, has seen progressive updates through the centuries, making a captivating document of varying trends in <a href="/wiki/English_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="English architecture">English architecture</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Middlesbrough_Transporter_Bridge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Middlesbrough_Transporter_Bridge.jpg/250px-Middlesbrough_Transporter_Bridge.jpg" width="250" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Middlesbrough_Transporter_Bridge.jpg/375px-Middlesbrough_Transporter_Bridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Middlesbrough_Transporter_Bridge.jpg/500px-Middlesbrough_Transporter_Bridge.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Middlesbrough_Transporter_Bridge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Transporter Bridge, built in 1911</div></div></div><p> Via a 1907 <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Parliament" title="Act of Parliament">Act of Parliament</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sir_William_Arrol_%26_Co." title="Sir William Arrol &amp; Co.">Sir William Arrol &amp; Co.</a> of Glasgow built the <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_Transporter_Bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Middlesbrough Transporter Bridge">Transporter Bridge</a> (1911) which spans the River Tees between Middlesbrough and <a href="/wiki/Port_Clarence" title="Port Clarence">Port Clarence</a>. At 850 feet (260&#160;m) long and 225 feet (69&#160;m) high, is one of the largest of its type in the world, and one of only two left in working order in Britain (the other being in <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Wales" title="Newport, Wales">Newport</a>). The bridge remains in daily use. It is, a Grade&#160;II* <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">listed building</a>.
</p><p>Another landmark, the <a href="/wiki/Tees_Newport_Bridge" title="Tees Newport Bridge">Tees Newport Bridge</a>, a vertical lift bridge, opened further along the river in 1934. Newport bridge still stands and is passable by traffic, but it can no longer lift the centre section.
</p><p>The urban centre of Middlesbrough remains home to a variety of architecture ranging from the <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_Institute_of_Modern_Art" title="Middlesbrough Institute of Modern Art">Middlesbrough Institute of Modern Art</a>, opened in January 2007 to replace a number of former outlying galleries; and <a href="/wiki/Centre_North_East" title="Centre North East">Centre North East</a>, formerly Corporation House, which opened in 1971. Many believe that there is a beauty to be found in the surrounding landscape of industry along the <a href="/wiki/River_Tees" title="River Tees">River Tees</a> from <a href="/wiki/Billingham" title="Billingham">Billingham</a> to Wilton. The terraced <a href="/wiki/Victorian_architecture" title="Victorian architecture">Victorian</a> streets surrounding the town centre are characterful elements of Middlesbrough's social and historical identity, and the vast streets surrounding Parliament Road and Abingdon Road a reminder of the area's wealth and rapid growth during industrialisation.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Middlesbrough_Town_Hall_Summer_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Middlesbrough_Town_Hall_Summer_2013.jpg/250px-Middlesbrough_Town_Hall_Summer_2013.jpg" width="250" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Middlesbrough_Town_Hall_Summer_2013.jpg/375px-Middlesbrough_Town_Hall_Summer_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Middlesbrough_Town_Hall_Summer_2013.jpg/500px-Middlesbrough_Town_Hall_Summer_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1990" data-file-height="1469" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Middlesbrough_Town_Hall_Summer_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_Town_Hall" title="Middlesbrough Town Hall">Middlesbrough Town Hall</a></div></div></div> <p><a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_Town_Hall" title="Middlesbrough Town Hall">Middlesbrough Town Hall</a>, designed by <a href="/wiki/George_Gordon_Hoskins" title="George Gordon Hoskins">George Gordon Hoskins</a> and built between 1883 and 1889 is a Grade&#160;II <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">listed building</a>, and a very imposing structure. Of comparable grandeur, is the Empire Palace of Varieties, of 1897, the finest surviving theatre edifice designed by Ernest Runtz in the UK. The first artist to star there in its guise as a <a href="/wiki/Music_hall" title="Music hall">music hall</a> was <a href="/wiki/Lillie_Langtry" title="Lillie Langtry">Lillie Langtry</a>. Later it became an early nightclub (1950s), then a bingo hall and is now once again a nightclub. Further afield, in Linthorpe, is the <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_Theatre" title="Middlesbrough Theatre">Middlesbrough Theatre</a> opened by Sir <a href="/wiki/John_Gielgud" title="John Gielgud">John Gielgud</a> in 1957; it was one of the first new theatres built in England after the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>.
</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boro_Central_Library_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Boro_Central_Library_2011.jpg/250px-Boro_Central_Library_2011.jpg" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Boro_Central_Library_2011.jpg/375px-Boro_Central_Library_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Boro_Central_Library_2011.jpg/500px-Boro_Central_Library_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boro_Central_Library_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Middlesbrough Central (Public) Library</div></div></div>
<p>The town includes England's only public sculpture by <a href="/wiki/Claes_Oldenburg" title="Claes Oldenburg">Claes Oldenburg</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> the "Bottle O' Notes" of 1993, which relates to <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">Captain James Cook</a>. Based alongside it today in the town's Central Gardens is the <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_Institute_of_Modern_Art" title="Middlesbrough Institute of Modern Art">Middlesbrough Institute of Modern Art</a> (MIMA). Refurbished in 2006, is the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_library" title="Carnegie library">Carnegie library</a>, dating from 1912. The Dorman Long office on Zetland Road, constructed between 1881 and 1891, is the only commercial building ever designed by <a href="/wiki/Philip_Webb" title="Philip Webb">Philip Webb</a>, the architect who worked for Sir Isaac Lowthian Bell.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Claes_Oldenburg%27s_Bottle_O%27_Notes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Claes_Oldenburg%27s_Bottle_O%27_Notes.jpg/220px-Claes_Oldenburg%27s_Bottle_O%27_Notes.jpg" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Claes_Oldenburg%27s_Bottle_O%27_Notes.jpg/330px-Claes_Oldenburg%27s_Bottle_O%27_Notes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Claes_Oldenburg%27s_Bottle_O%27_Notes.jpg/440px-Claes_Oldenburg%27s_Bottle_O%27_Notes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="4272" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Claes_Oldenburg%27s_Bottle_O%27_Notes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Claes Oldenburg's 'Bottle O' Notes' sculpture in Middlesbrough</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Temenos_Sculpture,_Middlesbrough.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Temenos_Sculpture%2C_Middlesbrough.jpg/250px-Temenos_Sculpture%2C_Middlesbrough.jpg" width="250" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Temenos_Sculpture%2C_Middlesbrough.jpg/375px-Temenos_Sculpture%2C_Middlesbrough.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Temenos_Sculpture%2C_Middlesbrough.jpg/500px-Temenos_Sculpture%2C_Middlesbrough.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4912" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Temenos_Sculpture,_Middlesbrough.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tees_Valley_Giants" title="Tees Valley Giants">Temenos</a> sculpture at Middlehaven.</div></div></div>
<p>Away from the town centre, at Middlehaven stands the <a href="/wiki/Tees_Valley_Giants" title="Tees Valley Giants">Temenos</a> sculpture, designed by sculptor <a href="/wiki/Anish_Kapoor" title="Anish Kapoor">Anish Kapoor</a> and designer <a href="/wiki/Cecil_Balmond" title="Cecil Balmond">Cecil Balmond</a>. The steel structure, consisting of a pole, a circular ring and an oval ring, stands approximately 110&#160;m long and 50&#160;m high and is held together by steel wire. It was unveiled in 2010 at a cost of £2.7&#160;million.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_leisure">Culture and leisure</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dorman_Museum_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Dorman_Museum_2011.jpg/220px-Dorman_Museum_2011.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Dorman_Museum_2011.jpg/330px-Dorman_Museum_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Dorman_Museum_2011.jpg/440px-Dorman_Museum_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dorman_Museum_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dorman Museum</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_Institute_of_Modern_Art" title="Middlesbrough Institute of Modern Art">Middlesbrough Institute of Modern Art</a> opened its doors in January 2007. It holds works by <a href="/wiki/Frank_Auerbach" title="Frank Auerbach">Frank Auerbach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tracey_Emin" title="Tracey Emin">Tracey Emin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paula_Rego" title="Paula Rego">Paula Rego</a> among others. Its considerable arts and crafts collections span from 1900 to the present day.
</p><p>Middlesbrough also has a healthy musical heritage. A number of bands and musicians hail from the area, including <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rodgers" title="Paul Rodgers">Paul Rodgers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Rea" title="Chris Rea">Chris Rea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Micky_Moody" title="Micky Moody">Micky Moody</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Middlesbrough_Institute_of_Modern_Art_-_MIMA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Middlesbrough_Institute_of_Modern_Art_-_MIMA.jpg/220px-Middlesbrough_Institute_of_Modern_Art_-_MIMA.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Middlesbrough_Institute_of_Modern_Art_-_MIMA.jpg/330px-Middlesbrough_Institute_of_Modern_Art_-_MIMA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Middlesbrough_Institute_of_Modern_Art_-_MIMA.jpg/440px-Middlesbrough_Institute_of_Modern_Art_-_MIMA.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3110" data-file-height="2051" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Middlesbrough_Institute_of_Modern_Art_-_MIMA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Middlesbrough Institute of Modern Art (mima)</div></div></div>
<p>Middlesbrough has two major recreational park spaces in <a href="/wiki/Albert_Park,_Middlesbrough" title="Albert Park, Middlesbrough">Albert Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stewart_Park,_Middlesbrough" title="Stewart Park, Middlesbrough">Stewart Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marton,_Middlesbrough" title="Marton, Middlesbrough">Marton</a>. Albert Park was donated to the town by Henry Bolckow in 1866. It was formally opened by <a href="/wiki/Prince_Arthur,_Duke_of_Connaught_and_Strathearn" title="Prince Arthur, Duke of Connaught and Strathearn">Prince Arthur</a> on 11 August 1868, and comprises a 30 hectares (74 acres) site. The park underwent a considerable period of restoration from 2001 to 2004, during which a number of the park's landmarks, saw either restoration or revival. Stewart Park was donated to the people of Middlesbrough in 1928 by Councillor Thomas Dormand Stewart and encompasses Victorian stable buildings, lakes and animal pens. During 2011 and 2012, the park underwent major refurbishment. Alongside these two parks are two of the town's cultural attractions, the century-old <a href="/wiki/Dorman_Memorial_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Dorman Memorial Museum">Dorman Memorial Museum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Captain_Cook_Birthplace_Museum" title="Captain Cook Birthplace Museum">Captain Cook Birthplace Museum</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Newham_Grange_Leisure_farm" class="mw-redirect" title="Newham Grange Leisure farm">Newham Grange Leisure farm</a> in Coulby Newham, one of the most southerly districts of the town, has operated continuously in this spot since the 17th century, becoming a leisure farm with the first residential development of the suburb in the 1970s. It is now a burgeoning tourist attraction: the chance to view its cattle, pigs, sheep and other farm animals is complemented by exhibitions of the farming history of the area.
</p><p>Middlesbrough is famous for the <a href="/wiki/Parmo" title="Parmo">Parmo</a>, a version of scallopini Parmigiana or schnitzel consisting of deep-fried breaded chicken or pork cutlet, topped with thick béchamel sauce and grilled cheese. It is usually served with chips, salad &amp; garlic sauce, with variations such as hotshot and fungi. Although it can be seen primarily as a takeaway dish, popular with Teessiders after a night out, it is also a popular restaurant dish with many establishments in around Teesside serving restaurant quality versions.
</p><p>In the Middlehaven ward, is the Transporter Bridge Visitor Centre, opened in 2000 and offering its own exhibitions charting the stirring past of the surrounding industrial powerhouse, as well as that of the singular structure it commemorates.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MFC_Riverside_Stadium.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/MFC_Riverside_Stadium.jpg/220px-MFC_Riverside_Stadium.jpg" width="220" height="60" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/MFC_Riverside_Stadium.jpg/330px-MFC_Riverside_Stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/MFC_Riverside_Stadium.jpg/440px-MFC_Riverside_Stadium.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6524" data-file-height="1775" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MFC_Riverside_Stadium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Riverside Stadium, 2015</div></div></div>
<p>Middlesbrough is home to the Championship <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> team, <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough F.C.</a>, owned by local haulage entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Steve_Gibson_(businessman)" title="Steve Gibson (businessman)">Steve Gibson</a>. The club is based at the <a href="/wiki/Riverside_Stadium" title="Riverside Stadium">Riverside Stadium</a> on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/River_Tees" title="River Tees">River Tees</a>, where they have played since moving from <a href="/wiki/Ayresome_Park" title="Ayresome Park">Ayresome Park</a>, their home for 92 years until 1995. Founder members of the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> in <a href="/wiki/FA_Premier_League_1992-93" class="mw-redirect" title="FA Premier League 1992-93">1992</a>, Middlesbrough won the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Cup">Football League Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/2004_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2004 Football League Cup Final">2004</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> and were beaten finalists in the <a href="/wiki/2005-06_UEFA_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="2005-06 UEFA Cup">2005-06 UEFA Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> In 1905 they made history with Britain's first £1,000 transfer when they signed <a href="/wiki/Alf_Common" title="Alf Common">Alf Common</a> from local rivals <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Proud_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proud-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Another league club, <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_Ironopolis_F.C." title="Middlesbrough Ironopolis F.C.">Middlesbrough Ironopolis F.C.</a>, was briefly based in the town in the late 19th century, but folded within a few years.
</p><p>Speedway racing was staged at Cleveland Park Stadium from the pioneer days of 1928 until the 1990s. The <a href="/wiki/Post-war" title="Post-war">post-war</a> team, known as The <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_Bears" title="Middlesbrough Bears">Middlesbrough Bears</a>, and for a time, The Teessiders, the Teesside Tigers and the Middlesbrough Tigers operated at all levels. The track operated for amateur speedway in the 1950s before re-opening in the Provincial League of 1961. The track closed for a spell later in the 1960s but returned in as members of the Second Division as The Teessiders.
</p><p>Middlesbrough is also represented nationally in <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">Futsal</a>. <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_Futsal_Club" title="Middlesbrough Futsal Club">Middlesbrough Futsal Club</a> play in the <a href="/wiki/FA_Futsal_League" class="mw-redirect" title="FA Futsal League">FA Futsal League</a> North, the national championship and their home games are played in Thornaby at Thornaby Pavilion.
</p><p>Athletics is a major sport in Middlesbrough with two local clubs serving Middlesbrough and the surrounding Teesside area, Middlesbrough and Cleveland Harriers and Middlesbrough AC (Mandale). Athletes used to regularly train at Clairville Stadium (1963-2014) until it was closed and subsequently demolished to make way for a housing development. Athletes now train at the recently opened (May 2015)<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Middlesbrough Sports Village, on Marton Road (A172). Notable athletes to train at both facilities are World &amp; European Indoor Sprint Champion Richard Kilty, British Indoor Long Jump record holder Chris Tomlinson and current British Internationals Matthew Hynes, Jonathon Taylor, Rabah Yousif and Amy Carr. The sports village includes a running track with grandstand, an indoor gym and cafe, football pitches, cycle circuit and a velodrome. Adjacent to the sports village is a skateboard plaza and also Middlesbrough Tennis World.
</p><p>Middlesbrough hosts several road races through the year. In September, the annual Middlesbrough Tees Pride 10k road race<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> is held on a one lap circuit round the southern part of the town. First held in 2005, the race now attracts several thousand competitors, from the serious club athlete to those in fancy dress raising money for local charities. Road races and training are also held regularly at Middlesbrough Cycle Circuit which is at the Middlesbrough Sports Village.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_RUFC" title="Middlesbrough RUFC">Middlesbrough RUFC</a> opened services in 1872, and are currently members of the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_1" title="Yorkshire 1">Yorkshire Division One</a>. They have played their home games at <a href="/wiki/Acklam_Park" title="Acklam Park">Acklam Park</a> since 1929, and have a ground-share with Middlesbrough Cricket Club, which commenced in 1930.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Middlesbrough" title="List of schools in Middlesbrough">List of schools in Middlesbrough</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Curve_Building,_Teesside_University.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/The_Curve_Building%2C_Teesside_University.JPG/220px-The_Curve_Building%2C_Teesside_University.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/The_Curve_Building%2C_Teesside_University.JPG/330px-The_Curve_Building%2C_Teesside_University.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/The_Curve_Building%2C_Teesside_University.JPG/440px-The_Curve_Building%2C_Teesside_University.JPG 2x" data-file-width="6048" data-file-height="4032" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Curve_Building,_Teesside_University.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Curve, Teesside University</div></div></div>
<p>Middlesbrough became a <a href="/wiki/College_town" title="College town">university town</a> in 1992, after a campaign<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (March 2013)">by whom?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> for a distinct "<a href="/wiki/Teesside_University" title="Teesside University">Teesside University</a>" since the 1960s. Before its establishment, extramural classes had been provided by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Leeds" title="University of Leeds">University of Leeds</a> <a href="/wiki/Adult_Education" class="mw-redirect" title="Adult Education">Adult Education Centre</a> on Harrow Road, from 1958 to 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Teesside University has more than 20,000 students. It dates back to 1930 as Constantine Technical College. Current departments of the university include Teesside University Business School and Schools of Arts and Media, Computing, Health and Social Care, Science &amp; Engineering and Social Sciences &amp; Law. The university teaches <a href="/wiki/Computer_animation" title="Computer animation">computer animation</a> and games design and co-hosts the annual <a href="/wiki/Animex_International_Festival_of_Animation_and_Computer_Games" title="Animex International Festival of Animation and Computer Games">Animex International Festival of Animation and Computer Games</a>. The university also has links with the <a href="/wiki/James_Cook_University_Hospital" title="James Cook University Hospital">James Cook University Hospital</a> south of the town centre.
</p><p>There are also modern schools, colleges and sixth forms colleges, the largest of which is <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_College" title="Middlesbrough College">Middlesbrough College</a>, in Middlehaven, with 16,000 students. Others include <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Catholic_College,_Middlesbrough" title="Trinity Catholic College, Middlesbrough">Trinity Catholic College</a> in Saltersgill<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Macmillan_Academy" title="Macmillan Academy">Macmillan Academy</a> on Stockton Road. <a href="/wiki/The_Northern_School_of_Art" title="The Northern School of Art">The Northern School of Art</a>, which opened in 1960, is also based in Middlesbrough and Hartlepool. It is one of only four specialist art and design further education colleges in the United Kingdom.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary_schools">Secondary schools</span></h3>
<p>Secondary schools in Middlesbrough include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Acklam_Grange_School" title="Acklam Grange School">Acklam Grange School</a>, also home to the Acorn Sports Centre ISHA</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Outwood_Academy_Acklam" title="Outwood Academy Acklam">Outwood Academy Acklam</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Trinity_Catholic_College,_Middlesbrough" title="Trinity Catholic College, Middlesbrough">Trinity Catholic College</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/The_King%27s_Academy,_Middlesbrough" title="The King&#39;s Academy, Middlesbrough">The King's Academy</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Unity_City_Academy" title="Unity City Academy">Unity City Academy</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Macmillan_Academy" title="Macmillan Academy">Macmillan Academy</a><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hillsview_Academy" title="Hillsview Academy">Hillsview Academy</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Outwood_Academy_Ormesby" title="Outwood Academy Ormesby">Outwood Academy Ormesby</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/St_Peter%27s_Catholic_Voluntary_Academy" title="St Peter&#39;s Catholic Voluntary Academy">St Peter's Catholic Voluntary Academy</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span></h2>
<p>In 2011, Middlesbrough had a population of 174,700,<sup id="cite_ref-Census2011_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2011-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> which makes it the largest town in <a href="/wiki/North_East_England" title="North East England">North East England</a> and largest urban <a href="/wiki/Human_settlement" title="Human settlement">settlement</a> within the non-administrative ceremonial county of <a href="/wiki/North_Yorkshire" title="North Yorkshire">North Yorkshire</a>. The borough had a population of 138,412 at the same census. For comparison, the Built-up area sub-division (BUASD) is about the same size as <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth" title="Bournemouth">Bournemouth</a>, the largest town in <a href="/wiki/South_West_England" title="South West England">South West England</a>. Middlesbrough town is larger than the borough. The town is made up of the borough, as well as the suburbs which make up the area known as <a href="/wiki/Greater_Eston" title="Greater Eston">Greater Eston</a>, which is to the east of the borough in <a href="/wiki/Redcar_and_Cleveland" title="Redcar and Cleveland">Redcar and Cleveland</a>. Greater Eston does not have a very high ethnic minority population, which makes the town less ethnically diverse than the smaller borough.
</p>
