<p><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the borough of Middlesbrough, 14.0% of the population were non-white British, compared with only 11.6% for the town. This makes the town about as ethnically diverse as <a href="/wiki/Exeter" title="Exeter">Exeter</a>. Additionally, it has a lower white British population than <a href="/wiki/Gateshead" title="Gateshead">Gateshead</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Shields" title="South Shields">South Shields</a> which are further north on the other side of <a href="/wiki/County_Durham" title="County Durham">County Durham</a>. It is also the second most ethnically diverse settlement in the North East (after Newcastle). The town of Middlesbrough is recognised as a Built-up area sub-division (BUASD) of <a href="/wiki/Teesside" title="Teesside">Teesside</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Office_for_National_Statistics" title="Office for National Statistics">Office for National Statistics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accent">Accent</span></h2>
<p>Middlesbrough English<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> is often grouped with the accents of North East England such as Geordie (spoken in Tyneside) and Mackem (spoken on Wearside) and occasionally with the accents of Yorkshire as it shares characteristics of both. Furthermore, the accent reflects the town's history. This accent is also known as a Smoggie accent or a Teesside accent.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Distinct_vowels">Distinct vowels</span></h3>
<p><i>Nurse/Square</i>
</p><p>A recognisable feature of Middlesbrough English is the fronted form of NURSE,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> reflecting its similarity with Liverpool English, having the characteristic NURSE/SQUARE merger at [ɛ:]. Additionally, the form is found to be the preferred variant of female speakers.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> This can be heard in words like work, purple, dirt and shirt which are pronounced more like "werk/wairk", "perple/pairple", "dert/dairt" and "shert/shairt". 
</p><p>Another feature of the Middlesbrough accent is the presence of a harsh "CK" sound. This indicates a possible influence from the many Welsh speakers that inhabited Middlesbrough at the same time as the Irish. Words such as black,track and crack often have an emphasis on the ck which give it a sound of clearing the throat. Not only is this feature prominent in Welsh speakers but it is also present in speakers from Liverpool. This further suggests the similarities between speakers from Middlesbrough and the Liverpool area.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Christianity">Christianity</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_John%27s_Church,_Middlesbrough-geograph-2129360.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/St_John%27s_Church%2C_Middlesbrough-geograph-2129360.jpg/220px-St_John%27s_Church%2C_Middlesbrough-geograph-2129360.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/St_John%27s_Church%2C_Middlesbrough-geograph-2129360.jpg/330px-St_John%27s_Church%2C_Middlesbrough-geograph-2129360.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/St_John%27s_Church%2C_Middlesbrough-geograph-2129360.jpg/440px-St_John%27s_Church%2C_Middlesbrough-geograph-2129360.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_John%27s_Church,_Middlesbrough-geograph-2129360.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>St John's Church</div></div></div>
<p>Middlesbrough is a <a href="/wiki/Deanery" title="Deanery">deanery</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Archdeaconry_of_Cleveland" class="mw-redirect" title="Archdeaconry of Cleveland">Archdeaconry of Cleveland</a>, a subdivision of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_York" title="Diocese of York">Diocese of York</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_York" title="Province of York">Province of York</a>. It stretches west from <a href="/wiki/Thirsk" title="Thirsk">Thirsk</a>, north to Middlesbrough, east to <a href="/wiki/Whitby" title="Whitby">Whitby</a> and south to <a href="/wiki/Pickering,_North_Yorkshire" title="Pickering, North Yorkshire">Pickering</a>.
</p><p>Middlesbrough is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Middlesbrough" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Middlesbrough">Roman Catholic Diocese of Middlesbrough</a>, which was created on 20 December 1878 from the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Beverley" title="Diocese of Beverley">Diocese of Beverley</a>. Middlesbrough is home to the Mother-Church of the diocese, <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_Cathedral" title="Middlesbrough Cathedral">St. Mary's Cathedral</a>, which is in the suburb of Coulby Newham and <a href="/wiki/Sacred_Heart_Church,_Middlesbrough" title="Sacred Heart Church, Middlesbrough">Sacred Heart Church</a> in the centre of the town. The present bishop is the Right Reverend Terence Patrick Drainey, 7th Bishop of Middlesbrough, who was ordained on Friday 25 January 2008.
</p><p>St Stephen's church, Middlesbrough, near the university campus, is a <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England_parish_church" title="Church of England parish church">Church of England parish church</a>, but is also in the Evangelical Connexion.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lugs_Lodge_Synagogue_-_geograph.org.uk_-_609300.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Lugs_Lodge_Synagogue_-_geograph.org.uk_-_609300.jpg/220px-Lugs_Lodge_Synagogue_-_geograph.org.uk_-_609300.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Lugs_Lodge_Synagogue_-_geograph.org.uk_-_609300.jpg/330px-Lugs_Lodge_Synagogue_-_geograph.org.uk_-_609300.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Lugs_Lodge_Synagogue_-_geograph.org.uk_-_609300.jpg/440px-Lugs_Lodge_Synagogue_-_geograph.org.uk_-_609300.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lugs_Lodge_Synagogue_-_geograph.org.uk_-_609300.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">synagogue</a> in Park Road South, which opened in 1938 and closed in 1998</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judaism">Judaism</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">Ashkenazi Jews</a> started to settle in Middlesbrough from 1862 and formed Middlesbrough Hebrew Congregation in 1870 with a <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">synagogue</a> in Hill Street. The synagogue moved to Brentnall Street in 1874 and then to a new building in 	
Park Road South in 1938.<sup id="cite_ref-JCR_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JCR-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Editions of the <i><a href="/wiki/Jewish_Year_Book" title="Jewish Year Book">Jewish Year Book</a></i> record the growth and decline of Middlesbrough's Jewish population. It was about 100 in 1896–97 and peaked at 750 in 1935. It then declined to 30 in 1998, in which year the synagogue in Park Road South was ceremonially closed.<sup id="cite_ref-JCR_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JCR-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islam">Islam</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islamic</a> community is represented in several mosques in Middlesbrough. <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> <a href="/wiki/Sailor" title="Sailor">sailors</a> visited Middlesbrough from about 1890.<sup id="cite_ref-multiple_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-multiple-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> and, in 1961, Azzam and Younis Din opened the first <a href="/wiki/Halal" title="Halal">Halal</a> <a href="/wiki/Butcher" title="Butcher">butcher</a> shop.<sup id="cite_ref-multiple_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-multiple-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The first <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosque</a> was a house in Grange Road in 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-multiple_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-multiple-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The Al-Madina Jamia Mosque, on Waterloo Road, the Dar ul Islam Central Mosque, on Southfield Road, and the Abu Bakr Mosque &amp; Community Centre,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> which is on Park Road North, are among the best known mosques in Middlesbrough today.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sikhism">Sikhism</span></h3>
<p>The Sikh community established its first gurdwara (temple) in Milton Street in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-multiple_51-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-multiple-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> After a time in Southfield Road, the centre is now in Lorne Street and was opened in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-multiple_51-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-multiple-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hinduism">Hinduism</span></h3>
<p>There is a Hindu Cultural Centre in Westbourne Grove, North Ormesby, which was opened in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-multiple_51-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-multiple-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Television_and_filmography">Television and filmography</span></h2>
<p>Middlesbrough has featured in many television programmes, including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fast_Show" title="The Fast Show">The Fast Show</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Inspector_George_Gently" title="Inspector George Gently">Inspector George Gently</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Steel_River_Blues" title="Steel River Blues">Steel River Blues</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Spender" title="Spender">Spender</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Play_for_Today" title="Play for Today">Play for Today</a></i> (<i>The Black Stuff</i>; latterly the drama <i><a href="/wiki/Boys_from_the_Blackstuff" title="Boys from the Blackstuff">Boys from the Blackstuff</a></i>) and <i><a href="/wiki/Auf_Wiedersehen,_Pet" title="Auf Wiedersehen, Pet">Auf Wiedersehen, Pet</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-visitmiddlesbrough.com_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visitmiddlesbrough.com-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Film director Ridley Scott is from the North East and based the opening shot of <i><a href="/wiki/Blade_Runner" title="Blade Runner">Blade Runner</a></i> on the view of the old ICI plant at Wilton. He said: “There’s a walk from Redcar … I’d cross a bridge at night, and walk above the steel works. So that’s probably where the opening of <i>Blade Runner</i> comes from. It always seemed to be rather gloomy and raining, and I’d just think “God, this is beautiful.” You can find beauty in everything, and so I think I found the beauty in that darkness.” Apparently the site was also considered as a shooting location for one of the sequels to Scott's Alien film.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Billy_Elliot" title="Billy Elliot">Billy Elliot</a></i> was filmed on the Middlesbrough Transporter Bridge.<sup id="cite_ref-visitmiddlesbrough.com_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visitmiddlesbrough.com-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2008, Middlesbrough was chosen as one of the sites in the BBC's <a href="/wiki/BBC_Big_Screen" title="BBC Big Screen">Public Space Broadcasting Project</a>. Like other towns participating in the project, Middlesbrough was offered a large 27&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (290&#160;sq&#160;ft) television screen by the BBC and the London Organising Committee of the Olympic Games. The screen was installed on 11 July 2008 and is at the western end of Centre Square.
</p><p>In the 2009 action thriller <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tournament_(2009_film)" title="The Tournament (2009 film)">The Tournament</a></i> Middlesbrough is that year's location where the assassins' competition is being held.
</p><p>In November 2009, the MiMA art gallery was used by the presenters of <i><a href="/wiki/Top_Gear_(2002_TV_series)" title="Top Gear (2002 TV series)">Top Gear</a></i> as part of a challenge. The challenge was to see if car exhibits would be more popular than normal art.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2013, Middlesbrough was used as a stand in for <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle</a> 1969 in BBC's <i><a href="/wiki/Inspector_George_Gently" title="Inspector George Gently">Inspector George Gently</a></i> starring <a href="/wiki/Martin_Shaw" title="Martin Shaw">Martin Shaw</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lee_Ingleby" title="Lee Ingleby">Lee Ingleby</a>; the footage appeared in the episode "Gently Between The Lines" (episode 1 of series 6).
</p><p>Reference is also made to Middlesbrough in works by London author Paul Breen including a work of fiction entitled "The Bones of a Season".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In 2010, filmmaker <a href="/wiki/John_Walsh_(filmmaker)" title="John Walsh (filmmaker)">John Walsh</a> made the satirical documentary <i><a href="/wiki/ToryBoy_The_Movie" title="ToryBoy The Movie">ToryBoy The Movie</a></i> about the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2010" title="United Kingdom general election, 2010">2010 general election</a> in <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Middlesbrough (UK Parliament constituency)">the Middlesbrough constituency</a> and sitting MP <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Bell" title="Stuart Bell">Stuart Bell</a>'s alleged laziness as an MP.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Middlesbrough" title="List of people from Middlesbrough">List of people from Middlesbrough</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Captainjamescookportrait.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Captainjamescookportrait.jpg/170px-Captainjamescookportrait.jpg" width="170" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Captainjamescookportrait.jpg/255px-Captainjamescookportrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Captainjamescookportrait.jpg/340px-Captainjamescookportrait.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1020" data-file-height="1280" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Captainjamescookportrait.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Captain James Cook, portrait by <a href="/wiki/Nathaniel_Dance-Holland" title="Nathaniel Dance-Holland">Nathaniel Dance</a>, c. 1775, <a href="/wiki/National_Maritime_Museum" title="National Maritime Museum">National Maritime Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenwich" title="Greenwich">Greenwich</a></div></div></div>
<p>Captain <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> (1728–79) the world-famous explorer, navigator, and cartographer was born in <a href="/wiki/Marton,_Middlesbrough" title="Marton, Middlesbrough">Marton</a>, now a suburb in the south of Middlesbrough.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tom_Dresser" title="Tom Dresser">Tom Dresser</a> (1892-1992), Middlesbrough's first Victoria Cross recipient during the First World War.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Stanley_Hollis" title="Stanley Hollis">Stanley Hollis</a> (1912–72), recipient of the only Victoria Cross awarded on <a href="/wiki/D-Day" class="mw-redirect" title="D-Day">D-Day</a> (6 June 1944).<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ellen_Wilkinson" title="Ellen Wilkinson">Ellen Wilkinson</a> was a famous MP for <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_East" class="mw-redirect" title="Middlesbrough East">Middlesbrough East</a>, and was the first female <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Education" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister of Education">Minister of Education</a>. She also wrote a novel <i>Clash</i> (1929) which paints a very positive picture of "Shireport" (Middlesbrough).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Steph_McGovern" title="Steph McGovern">Steph McGovern</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Business_journalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Business journalist">business journalist</a> for the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>, grew up in Middlesbrough.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Marion_Coates_Hansen" title="Marion Coates Hansen">Marion Coates Hansen</a> was an active member of the local <a href="/wiki/Independent_Labour_Party" title="Independent Labour Party">Independent Labour Party</a> (ILP). She was a feminist and women's suffrage campaigner, an early member of the militant <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Social_and_Political_Union" title="Women&#39;s Social and Political Union">Women's Social and Political Union</a> (WSPU) and a founder member of the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Freedom_League" title="Women&#39;s Freedom League">Women's Freedom League</a> (WFL) in 1907.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Maud_Chadburn" title="Maud Chadburn">Maud Chadburn</a> was one of the earliest women in the United Kingdom to pursue a career as a surgeon. She also co-founded the <a href="/wiki/South_London_Hospital_for_Women_and_Children" title="South London Hospital for Women and Children">South London Hospital for Women and Children</a> in 1912 with fellow surgeon Eleanor Davies-Colley.
</p><p>Other famous people from Middlesbrough include:
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_arts">The arts</span></h3>
<ul><li>Models <a href="/wiki/Jade_McSorley" title="Jade McSorley">Jade McSorley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Preeti_Desai" title="Preeti Desai">Preeti Desai</a>, who was Miss Great Britain 2006</li>
<li>Comedians <a href="/wiki/Dave_Morris_(comedian)" title="Dave Morris (comedian)">Dave Morris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Mortimer" title="Bob Mortimer">Bob Mortimer</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roy_Chubby_Brown" title="Roy Chubby Brown">Roy Chubby Brown</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Connelly" title="Kevin Connelly">Kevin Connelly</a></li>
<li>Musicians <a href="/wiki/Ron_Aspery" class="mw-redirect" title="Ron Aspery">Ron Aspery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyril_Smith_(pianist)" title="Cyril Smith (pianist)">Cyril Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Rea" title="Chris Rea">Chris Rea</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rodgers" title="Paul Rodgers">Paul Rodgers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Micky_Moody" title="Micky Moody">Micky Moody</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alistair_Griffin" title="Alistair Griffin">Alistair Griffin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vin_Garbutt" title="Vin Garbutt">Vin Garbutt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Corner" title="Chris Corner">Chris Corner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Thomas" title="Bruce Thomas">Bruce Thomas</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Arthur" title="James Arthur">James Arthur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pete_Trewavas" title="Pete Trewavas">Pete Trewavas</a></li>
<li>Actors <a href="/wiki/Thelma_Barlow" title="Thelma Barlow">Thelma Barlow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Bentley" title="Marcus Bentley">Marcus Bentley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Benton" title="Mark Benton">Mark Benton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sean_Blowers" title="Sean Blowers">Sean Blowers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Carling" title="Elizabeth Carling">Elizabeth Carling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alethea_Charlton" title="Alethea Charlton">Alethea Charlton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Preeti_Desai" title="Preeti Desai">Preeti Desai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Desmonde" title="Jerry Desmonde">Jerry Desmonde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monica_Dolan" title="Monica Dolan">Monica Dolan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neil_Grainger" title="Neil Grainger">Neil Grainger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lila_Kaye" title="Lila Kaye">Lila Kaye</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faye_Marsay" title="Faye Marsay">Faye Marsay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Quinten" title="Christopher Quinten">Christopher Quinten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wendy_Richard" title="Wendy Richard">Wendy Richard</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Telfer" title="John Telfer">John Telfer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Parker" title="Jamie Parker">Jamie Parker</a>.</li>
<li>Writers <a href="/wiki/Ann_Jellicoe" title="Ann Jellicoe">Ann Jellicoe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Milward" title="Richard Milward">Richard Milward</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wally_K_Daly" class="mw-redirect" title="Wally K Daly">Wally K Daly</a></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_entertainers">Other entertainers</span></h3>
<ul><li>Magicians <a href="/wiki/Martin_Daniels" title="Martin Daniels">Martin Daniels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Daniels" title="Paul Daniels">Paul Daniels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pete_Firman" title="Pete Firman">Pete Firman</a></li>
<li>TV presenter <a href="/wiki/Kirsten_O%27Brien" title="Kirsten O&#39;Brien">Kirsten O'Brien</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Kay Murray</li>
<li>Radio presenter <a href="/wiki/Ali_Brownlee" title="Ali Brownlee">Ali Brownlee</a></li>
<li>Magician/comedian <a href="/wiki/John_Archer_(magician)" title="John Archer (magician)">John Archer</a></li>
<li>Singer <a href="/wiki/Marion_Ryan" title="Marion Ryan">Marion Ryan</a></li></ul>
<p>Other eminent sons and daughters of Middlesbrough and its environs include <a href="/wiki/Martin_Narey" title="Martin Narey">Sir Martin Narey</a> (1955–present), former Director General of the Prison Service and chief executive of Barnardo's, Professor Sir <a href="/wiki/Liam_Donaldson" title="Liam Donaldson">Liam Donaldson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Chief Medical Officer for England, <a href="/wiki/Ernest_William_Hornung" class="mw-redirect" title="Ernest William Hornung">E. W. Hornung</a>, the creator of the gentleman-crook Raffles (who was fluent in three Yorkshire dialects), and <a href="/wiki/Naomi_Jacob" title="Naomi Jacob">Naomi Jacob</a> novelist. <a href="/wiki/Cyril_Smith_(pianist)" title="Cyril Smith (pianist)">Cyril Smith</a> (1909–74), the concert pianist. Two immigrant sons – Frank and Edgar Watts – opened the English Hotel in the <a href="/wiki/Cumberland_Gap" title="Cumberland Gap">Cumberland Gap</a> which gave their hometown's name to <a href="/wiki/Middlesboro,_Kentucky" title="Middlesboro, Kentucky">Middlesboro, Kentucky</a>, in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The classic study, <i>At The Works</i> (1907), by <a href="/wiki/Florence_Bell_(writer)" title="Florence Bell (writer)">Florence Bell</a> (1851–1930), gives a picture of the area at the turn of the 20th century. She also edited the letters of her stepdaughter <a href="/wiki/Gertrude_Bell" title="Gertrude Bell">Gertrude Bell</a> (1868–1926), which has been continuously in print since 1927. <a href="/wiki/Pat_Barker" title="Pat Barker">Pat Barker</a>'s debut novel <i>Union Street</i> was set on the thoroughfare of the same name in the town. The Jonny Briggs series of books, written by <a href="/wiki/Joan_Eadington" title="Joan Eadington">Joan Eadington</a> and later to become a <a href="/wiki/Jonny_Briggs" title="Jonny Briggs">BBC Children's TV series</a> of the same name, was also based in the town. <a href="/wiki/David_Shayler" title="David Shayler">David Shayler</a>, the ex-spy, journalist and <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_theorist" class="mw-redirect" title="Conspiracy theorist">conspiracy theorist</a>, was born in Middlesbrough.<sup id="cite_ref-DStoFootie_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DStoFootie-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ford_Madox_Ford" title="Ford Madox Ford">Ford Madox Ford</a> (1873–1939) was billeted in <a href="/wiki/Eston" title="Eston">Eston</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Great_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Great War">Great War</a> (1914–18), and his great <a href="/wiki/Novel_sequence" title="Novel sequence">novel sequence</a> <i>Parade's End</i> is partly set in Busby Hall, <a href="/wiki/Little_Busby" title="Little Busby">Little Busby</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Carlton-in-Cleveland" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlton-in-Cleveland">Carlton-in-Cleveland</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Adrian_Warburton" title="Adrian Warburton">Adrian "Six Medals" Warburton</a>, air photographer, was played by <a href="/wiki/Alec_Guinness" title="Alec Guinness">Alec Guinness</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Malta_Story" title="Malta Story">Malta Story</a></i>.
</p><p>The great model maker <a href="/wiki/Richard_Old" title="Richard Old">Richard Old</a> (1856–1932) resided for most of his life at 6&#160;Ruby Street.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns">Twin towns</span></h2>
<p>Middlesbrough is <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a> with:
</p>
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Middlesboro,_Kentucky" title="Middlesboro, Kentucky">Middlesboro, Kentucky</a>, USA<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe"><img alt="Zimbabwe" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg/23px-Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg/35px-Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg/46px-Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="840" data-file-height="420" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Masvingo" title="Masvingo">Masvingo</a>, Zimbabwe, since 1990<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany"><img alt="Germany" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Oberhausen" title="Oberhausen">Oberhausen</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="North Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</a>, Germany, since 1974<sup id="cite_ref-Middlesbrough_twinning_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Middlesbrough_twinning-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/France" title="France"><img alt="France" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Dunkirk" title="Dunkirk">Dunkirk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nord_(French_department)" title="Nord (French department)">Nord</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hauts-de-France" title="Hauts-de-France">Hauts-de-France</a>, France<sup id="cite_ref-Archant_twinning_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archant_twinning-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
